org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Time;\\n80: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Timer;\\n81: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils;\\n82: \\n83: import org.slf4j.Logger;\\n84: \\n85: import java.net.InetSocketAddress;\\n86: import java.time.Duration;\\n87: import java.util.Arrays;\\n88: import java.util.Collections;\\n89: import java.util.List;\\n90: import java.util.Map;\\n91: import java.util.Objects;\\n92: import java.util.Optional;\\n93: import java.util.Properties;\\n94: import java.util.concurrent.ExecutionException;\\n95: import java.util.concurrent.Future;\\n96: import java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\\n97: import java.util.concurrent.atomic.AtomicReference;\\n98: \\n99: \\n100: /**\\n101:  * A Kafka client that publishes records to the Kafka cluster.\\n102:  * <P>\\n103:  * The producer is <i>thread safe</i> and sharing a single producer instance across threads will generally be faster than\\n104:  * having multiple instances.\\n105:  * <p>\\n106:  * Here is a simple example of using the producer to send records with strings containing sequential numbers as the key/value\\n107:  * pairs.\\n108:  * <pre>\\n109:  * {@code\\n110:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n111:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n112:  * props.put(\\\"linger.ms\\\", 1);\\n113:  * props.put(\\\"key.serializer\\\", \\\"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\\\");\\n114:  * props.put(\\\"value.serializer\\\", \\\"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\\\");\\n115:  *\\n116:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props);\\n117:  * for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\\n118:  *     producer.send(new ProducerRecord<String, String>(\\\"my-topic\\\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\\n119:  *\\n120:  * producer.close();\\n121:  * }</pre>\\n122:  * <p>\\n123:  * The producer consists of a pool of buffer space that holds records that haven't yet been transmitted to the server\\n124:  * as well as a background I/O thread that is responsible for turning these records into requests and transmitting them\\n125:  * to the cluster. Failure to close the producer after use will leak these resources.\\n126:  * <p>\\n127:  * The {@link #send(ProducerRecord) send()} method is asynchronous. When called, it adds the record to a buffer of pending record sends\\n128:  * and immediately returns. This allows the producer to batch together individual records for efficiency.\\n129:  * <p>\\n130:  * The <code>acks</code> config controls the criteria under which requests are considered complete. The default setting \\\"all\\\"\\n131:  * will result in blocking on the full commit of the record, the slowest but most durable setting.\\n132:  * <p>\\n133:  * If the request fails, the producer can automatically retry. The <code>retries</code> setting defaults to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>, and\\n134:  * it's recommended to use <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> to control retry behavior, instead of <code>retries</code>.\\n135:  * <p>\\n136:  * The producer maintains buffers of unsent records for each partition. These buffers are of a size specified by\\n137:  * the <code>batch.size</code> config. Making this larger can result in more batching, but requires more memory (since we will\\n138:  * generally have one of these buffers for each active partition).\\n139:  * <p>\\n140:  * By default a buffer is available to send immediately even if there is additional unused space in the buffer. However if you\\n141:  * want to reduce the number of requests you can set <code>linger.ms</code> to something greater than 0. This will\\n142:  * instruct the producer to wait up to that number of milliseconds before sending a request in hope that more records will\\n143:  * arrive to fill up the same batch. This is analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. For example, in the code snippet above,\\n144:  * likely all 100 records would be sent in a single request since we set our linger time to 1 millisecond. However this setting\\n145:  * would add 1 millisecond of latency to our request waiting for more records to arrive if we didn't fill up the buffer. Note that\\n146:  * records that arrive close together in time will generally batch together even with <code>linger.ms=0</code>. So, under heavy load,\\n147:  * batching will occur regardless of the linger configuration; however setting this to something larger than 0 can lead to fewer, more\\n148:  * efficient requests when not under maximal load at the cost of a small amount of latency.\\n149:  * <p>\\n150:  * The <code>buffer.memory</code> controls the total amount of memory available to the producer for buffering. If records\\n151:  * are sent faster than they can be transmitted to the server then this buffer space will be exhausted. When the buffer space is\\n152:  * exhausted additional send calls will block. The threshold for time to block is determined by <code>max.block.ms</code> after which it returns\\n153:  * a failed future with BufferExhaustedException.\\n154:  * <p>\\n155:  * The <code>key.serializer</code> and <code>value.serializer</code> instruct how to turn the key and value objects the user provides with\\n156:  * their <code>ProducerRecord</code> into bytes. You can use the included {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.ByteArraySerializer} or\\n157:  * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer} for simple byte or string types.\\n158:  * <p>\\n159:  * From Kafka 0.11, the KafkaProducer supports two additional modes: the idempotent producer and the transactional producer.\\n160:  * The idempotent producer strengthens Kafka's delivery semantics from at least once to exactly once delivery. In particular\\n161:  * producer retries will no longer introduce duplicates. The transactional producer allows an application to send messages\\n162:  * to multiple partitions (and topics!) atomically.\\n163:  * </p>\\n164:  * <p>\\n165:  * From Kafka 3.0, the <code>enable.idempotence</code> configuration defaults to true. When enabling idempotence,\\n166:  * <code>retries</code> config will default to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code> and the <code>acks</code> config will\\n167:  * default to <code>all</code>. There are no API changes for the idempotent producer, so existing applications will\\n168:  * not need to be modified to take advantage of this feature.\\n169:  * </p>\\n170:  * <p>\\n171:  * To take advantage of the idempotent producer, it is imperative to avoid application level re-sends since these cannot\\n172:  * be de-duplicated. As such, if an application enables idempotence, it is recommended to leave the <code>retries</code>\\n173:  * config unset, as it will be defaulted to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>. Additionally, if a {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n174:  * returns an error even with infinite retries (for instance if the message expires in the buffer before being sent),\\n175:  * then it is recommended to shut down the producer and check the contents of the last produced message to ensure that\\n176:  * it is not duplicated. Finally, the producer can only guarantee idempotence for messages sent within a single session.\\n177:  * </p>\\n178:  * <p>To use the transactional producer and the attendant APIs, you must set the <code>transactional.id</code>\\n179:  * configuration property. If the <code>transactional.id</code> is set, idempotence is automatically enabled along with\\n180:  * the producer configs which idempotence depends on. Further, topics which are included in transactions should be configured\\n181:  * for durability. In particular, the <code>replication.factor</code> should be at least <code>3</code>, and the\\n182:  * <code>min.insync.replicas</code> for these topics should be set to 2. Finally, in order for transactional guarantees\\n183:  * to be realized from end-to-end, the consumers must be configured to read only committed messages as well.\\n184:  * </p>\\n185:  * <p>\\n186:  * The purpose of the <code>transactional.id</code> is to enable transaction recovery across multiple sessions of a\\n187:  * single producer instance. It would typically be derived from the shard identifier in a partitioned, stateful, application.\\n188:  * As such, it should be unique to each producer instance running within a partitioned application.\\n189:  * </p>\\n190:  * <p>All the new transactional APIs are blocking and will throw exceptions on failure. The example\\n191:  * below illustrates how the new APIs are meant to be used. It is similar to the example above, except that all\\n192:  * 100 messages are part of a single transaction.\\n193:  * </p>\\n194:  * <p>\\n195:  * <pre>\\n196:  * {@code\\n197:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n198:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n199:  * props.put(\\\"transactional.id\\\", \\\"my-transactional-id\\\");\\n200:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props, new StringSerializer(), new StringSerializer());\\n201:  *\\n202:  * producer.initTransactions();\\n203:  *\\n204:  * try {\\n205:  *     producer.beginTransaction();\\n206:  *     for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\\n207:  *         producer.send(new ProducerRecord<>(\\\"my-topic\\\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\\n208:  *     producer.commitTransaction();\\n209:  * } catch (ProducerFencedException | OutOfOrderSequenceException | AuthorizationException e) {\\n210:  *     // We can't recover from these exceptions, so our only option is to close the producer and exit.\\n211:  *     producer.close();\\n212:  * } catch (KafkaException e) {\\n213:  *     // For all other exceptions, just abort the transaction and try again.\\n214:  *     producer.abortTransaction();\\n215:  * }\\n216:  * producer.close();\\n217:  * } </pre>\\n218:  * </p>\\n219:  * <p>\\n220:  * As is hinted at in the example, there can be only one open transaction per producer. All messages sent between the\\n221:  * {@link #beginTransaction()} and {@link #commitTransaction()} calls will be part of a single transaction. When the\\n222:  * <code>transactional.id</code> is specified, all messages sent by the producer must be part of a transaction.\\n223:  * </p>\\n224:  * <p>\\n225:  * The transactional producer uses exceptions to communicate error states. In particular, it is not required\\n226:  * to specify callbacks for <code>producer.send()</code> or to call <code>.get()</code> on the returned Future: a\\n227:  * <code>KafkaException</code> would be thrown if any of the\\n228:  * <code>producer.send()</code> or transactional calls hit an irrecoverable error during a transaction. See the {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n229:  * documentation for more details about detecting errors from a transactional send.\\n230:  * </p>\\n231:  * </p>By calling\\n232:  * <code>producer.abortTransaction()</code> upon receiving a <code>KafkaException</code> we can ensure that any\\n233:  * successful writes are marked as aborted, hence keeping the transactional guarantees.\\n234:  * </p>\\n235:  * <p>\\n236:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\\n237:  * certain client features.  For instance, the transactional APIs need broker versions 0.11.0 or later. You will receive an\\n238:  * <code>UnsupportedVersionException</code> when invoking an API that is not available in the running broker version.\\n239:  * </p>\\n240:  */\\n241: public class java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\\n97: import java.util.concurrent.atomic.AtomicReference;\\n98: \\n99: \\n100: /**\\n101:  * A Kafka client that publishes records to the Kafka cluster.\\n102:  * <P>\\n103:  * The producer is <i>thread safe</i> and sharing a single producer instance across threads will generally be faster than\\n104:  * having multiple instances.\\n105:  * <p>\\n106:  * Here is a simple example of using the producer to send records with strings containing sequential numbers as the key/value\\n107:  * pairs.\\n108:  * <pre>\\n109:  * {@code\\n110:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n111:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n112:  * props.put(\\\"linger.ms\\\", 1);\\n113:  * props.put(\\\"key.serializer\\\", \\\"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\\\");\\n114:  * props.put(\\\"value.serializer\\\", \\\"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\\\");\\n115:  *\\n116:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props);\\n117:  * for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\\n118:  *     producer.send(new ProducerRecord<String, String>(\\\"my-topic\\\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\\n119:  *\\n120:  * producer.close();\\n121:  * }</pre>\\n122:  * <p>\\n123:  * The producer consists of a pool of buffer space that holds records that haven't yet been transmitted to the server\\n124:  * as well as a background I/O thread that is responsible for turning these records into requests and transmitting them\\n125:  * to the cluster. Failure to close the producer after use will leak these resources.\\n126:  * <p>\\n127:  * The {@link #send(ProducerRecord) send()} method is asynchronous. When called, it adds the record to a buffer of pending record sends\\n128:  * and immediately returns. This allows the producer to batch together individual records for efficiency.\\n129:  * <p>\\n130:  * The <code>acks</code> config controls the criteria under which requests are considered complete. The default setting \\\"all\\\"\\n131:  * will result in blocking on the full commit of the record, the slowest but most durable setting.\\n132:  * <p>\\n133:  * If the request fails, the producer can automatically retry. The <code>retries</code> setting defaults to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>, and\\n134:  * it's recommended to use <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> to control retry behavior, instead of <code>retries</code>.\\n135:  * <p>\\n136:  * The producer maintains buffers of unsent records for each partition. These buffers are of a size specified by\\n137:  * the <code>batch.size</code> config. Making this larger can result in more batching, but requires more memory (since we will\\n138:  * generally have one of these buffers for each active partition).\\n139:  * <p>\\n140:  * By default a buffer is available to send immediately even if there is additional unused space in the buffer. However if you\\n141:  * want to reduce the number of requests you can set <code>linger.ms</code> to something greater than 0. This will\\n142:  * instruct the producer to wait up to that number of milliseconds before sending a request in hope that more records will\\n143:  * arrive to fill up the same batch. This is analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. For example, in the code snippet above,\\n144:  * likely all 100 records would be sent in a single request since we set our linger time to 1 millisecond. However this setting\\n145:  * would add 1 millisecond of latency to our request waiting for more records to arrive if we didn't fill up the buffer. Note that\\n146:  * records that arrive close together in time will generally batch together even with <code>linger.ms=0</code>. So, under heavy load,\\n147:  * batching will occur regardless of the linger configuration; however setting this to something larger than 0 can lead to fewer, more\\n148:  * efficient requests when not under maximal load at the cost of a small amount of latency.\\n149:  * <p>\\n150:  * The <code>buffer.memory</code> controls the total amount of memory available to the producer for buffering. If records\\n151:  * are sent faster than they can be transmitted to the server then this buffer space will be exhausted. When the buffer space is\\n152:  * exhausted additional send calls will block. The threshold for time to block is determined by <code>max.block.ms</code> after which it returns\\n153:  * a failed future with BufferExhaustedException.\\n154:  * <p>\\n155:  * The <code>key.serializer</code> and <code>value.serializer</code> instruct how to turn the key and value objects the user provides with\\n156:  * their <code>ProducerRecord</code> into bytes. You can use the included {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.ByteArraySerializer} or\\n157:  * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer} for simple byte or string types.\\n158:  * <p>\\n159:  * From Kafka 0.11, the KafkaProducer supports two additional modes: the idempotent producer and the transactional producer.\\n160:  * The idempotent producer strengthens Kafka's delivery semantics from at least once to exactly once delivery. In particular\\n161:  * producer retries will no longer introduce duplicates. The transactional producer allows an application to send messages\\n162:  * to multiple partitions (and topics!) atomically.\\n163:  * </p>\\n164:  * <p>\\n165:  * From Kafka 3.0, the <code>enable.idempotence</code> configuration defaults to true. When enabling idempotence,\\n166:  * <code>retries</code> config will default to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code> and the <code>acks</code> config will\\n167:  * default to <code>all</code>. There are no API changes for the idempotent producer, so existing applications will\\n168:  * not need to be modified to take advantage of this feature.\\n169:  * </p>\\n170:  * <p>\\n171:  * To take advantage of the idempotent producer, it is imperative to avoid application level re-sends since these cannot\\n172:  * be de-duplicated. As such, if an application enables idempotence, it is recommended to leave the <code>retries</code>\\n173:  * config unset, as it will be defaulted to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>. Additionally, if a {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n174:  * returns an error even with infinite retries (for instance if the message expires in the buffer before being sent),\\n175:  * then it is recommended to shut down the producer and check the contents of the last produced message to ensure that\\n176:  * it is not duplicated. Finally, the producer can only guarantee idempotence for messages sent within a single session.\\n177:  * </p>\\n178:  * <p>To use the transactional producer and the attendant APIs, you must set the <code>transactional.id</code>\\n179:  * configuration property. If the <code>transactional.id</code> is set, idempotence is automatically enabled along with\\n180:  * the producer configs which idempotence depends on. Further, topics which are included in transactions should be configured\\n181:  * for durability. In particular, the <code>replication.factor</code> should be at least <code>3</code>, and the\\n182:  * <code>min.insync.replicas</code> for these topics should be set to 2. Finally, in order for transactional guarantees\\n183:  * to be realized from end-to-end, the consumers must be configured to read only committed messages as well.\\n184:  * </p>\\n185:  * <p>\\n186:  * The purpose of the <code>transactional.id</code> is to enable transaction recovery across multiple sessions of a\\n187:  * single producer instance. It would typically be derived from the shard identifier in a partitioned, stateful, application.\\n188:  * As such, it should be unique to each producer instance running within a partitioned application.\\n189:  * </p>\\n190:  * <p>All the new transactional APIs are blocking and will throw exceptions on failure. The example\\n191:  * below illustrates how the new APIs are meant to be used. It is similar to the example above, except that all\\n192:  * 100 messages are part of a single transaction.\\n193:  * </p>\\n194:  * <p>\\n195:  * <pre>\\n196:  * {@code\\n197:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n198:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n199:  * props.put(\\\"transactional.id\\\", \\\"my-transactional-id\\\");\\n200:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props, new StringSerializer(), new StringSerializer());\\n201:  *\\n202:  * producer.initTransactions();\\n203:  *\\n204:  * try {\\n205:  *     producer.beginTransaction();\\n206:  *     for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\\n207:  *         producer.send(new ProducerRecord<>(\\\"my-topic\\\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\\n208:  *     producer.commitTransaction();\\n209:  * } catch (ProducerFencedException | OutOfOrderSequenceException | AuthorizationException e) {\\n210:  *     // We can't recover from these exceptions, so our only option is to close the producer and exit.\\n211:  *     producer.close();\\n212:  * } catch (KafkaException e) {\\n213:  *     // For all other exceptions, just abort the transaction and try again.\\n214:  *     producer.abortTransaction();\\n215:  * }\\n216:  * producer.close();\\n217:  * } </pre>\\n218:  * </p>\\n219:  * <p>\\n220:  * As is hinted at in the example, there can be only one open transaction per producer. All messages sent between the\\n221:  * {@link #beginTransaction()} and {@link #commitTransaction()} calls will be part of a single transaction. When the\\n222:  * <code>transactional.id</code> is specified, all messages sent by the producer must be part of a transaction.\\n223:  * </p>\\n224:  * <p>\\n225:  * The transactional producer uses exceptions to communicate error states. In particular, it is not required\\n226:  * to specify callbacks for <code>producer.send()</code> or to call <code>.get()</code> on the returned Future: a\\n227:  * <code>KafkaException</code> would be thrown if any of the\\n228:  * <code>producer.send()</code> or transactional calls hit an irrecoverable error during a transaction. See the {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n229:  * documentation for more details about detecting errors from a transactional send.\\n230:  * </p>\\n231:  * </p>By calling\\n232:  * <code>producer.abortTransaction()</code> upon receiving a <code>KafkaException</code> we can ensure that any\\n233:  * successful writes are marked as aborted, hence keeping the transactional guarantees.\\n234:  * </p>\\n235:  * <p>\\n236:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\\n237:  * certain client features.  For instance, the transactional APIs need broker versions 0.11.0 or later. You will receive an\\n238:  * <code>UnsupportedVersionException</code> when invoking an API that is not available in the running broker version.\\n239:  * </p>\\n240:  */\\n241: public class java.net.InetSocketAddress;\n86: import java.time.Duration;\n87: import java.util.Arrays;\n88: import java.util.Collections;\n89: import java.util.List;\n90: import java.util.Map;\n91: import java.util.Objects;\n92: import java.util.Optional;\n93: import java.util.Properties;\n94: import java.util.concurrent.ExecutionException;\n95: import java.util.concurrent.Future;\n96: import java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\n97: import java.util.concurrent.atomic.AtomicReference;\n98: \n99: \n100: /**\n101:  * A Kafka client that publishes records to the Kafka cluster.\n102:  * <P>\n103:  * The producer is <i>thread safe</i> and sharing a single producer instance across threads will generally be faster than\n104:  * having multiple instances.\n105:  * <p>\n106:  * Here is a simple example of using the producer to send records with strings containing sequential numbers as the key/value\n107:  * pairs.\n108:  * <pre>\n109:  * {@code\n110:  * Properties props = new Properties();\n111:  * props.put(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n112:  * props.put(\"linger.ms\", 1);\n113:  * props.put(\"key.serializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\");\n114:  * props.put(\"value.serializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\");\n115:  *\n116:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props);\n117:  * for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\n118:  *     producer.send(new ProducerRecord<String, String>(\"my-topic\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\n119:  *\n120:  * producer.close();\n121:  * }</pre>\n122:  * <p>\n123:  * The producer consists of a pool of buffer space that holds records that haven't yet been transmitted to the server\n124:  * as well as a background I/O thread that is responsible for turning these records into requests and transmitting them\n125:  * to the cluster. Failure to close the producer after use will leak these resources.\n126:  * <p>\n127:  * The {@link #send(ProducerRecord) send()} method is asynchronous. When called, it adds the record to a buffer of pending record sends\n128:  * and immediately returns. This allows the producer to batch together individual records for efficiency.\n129:  * <p>\n130:  * The <code>acks</code> config controls the criteria under which requests are considered complete. The default setting \"all\"\n131:  * will result in blocking on the full commit of the record, the slowest but most durable setting.\n132:  * <p>\n133:  * If the request fails, the producer can automatically retry. The <code>retries</code> setting defaults to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>, and\n134:  * it's recommended to use <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> to control retry behavior, instead of <code>retries</code>.\n135:  * <p>\n136:  * The producer maintains buffers of unsent records for each partition. These buffers are of a size specified by\n137:  * the <code>batch.size</code> config. Making this larger can result in more batching, but requires more memory (since we will\n138:  * generally have one of these buffers for each active partition).\n139:  * <p>\n140:  * By default a buffer is available to send immediately even if there is additional unused space in the buffer. However if you\n141:  * want to reduce the number of requests you can set <code>linger.ms</code> to something greater than 0. This will\n142:  * instruct the producer to wait up to that number of milliseconds before sending a request in hope that more records will\n143:  * arrive to fill up the same batch. This is analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. For example, in the code snippet above,\n144:  * likely all 100 records would be sent in a single request since we set our linger time to 1 millisecond. However this setting\n145:  * would add 1 millisecond of latency to our request waiting for more records to arrive if we didn't fill up the buffer. Note that\n146:  * records that arrive close together in time will generally batch together even with <code>linger.ms=0</code>. So, under heavy load,\n147:  * batching will occur regardless of the linger configuration; however setting this to something larger than 0 can lead to fewer, more\n148:  * efficient requests when not under maximal load at the cost of a small amount of latency.\n149:  * <p>\n150:  * The <code>buffer.memory</code> controls the total amount of memory available to the producer for buffering. If records\n151:  * are sent faster than they can be transmitted to the server then this buffer space will be exhausted. When the buffer space is\n152:  * exhausted additional send calls will block. The threshold for time to block is determined by <code>max.block.ms</code> after which it returns\n153:  * a failed future with BufferExhaustedException.\n154:  * <p>\n155:  * The <code>key.serializer</code> and <code>value.serializer</code> instruct how to turn the key and value objects the user provides with\n156:  * their <code>ProducerRecord</code> into bytes. You can use the included {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.ByteArraySerializer} or\n157:  * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer} for simple byte or string types.\n158:  * <p>\n159:  * From Kafka 0.11, the KafkaProducer supports two additional modes: the idempotent producer and the transactional producer.\n160:  * The idempotent producer strengthens Kafka's delivery semantics from at least once to exactly once delivery. In particular\n161:  * producer retries will no longer introduce duplicates. The transactional producer allows an application to send messages\n162:  * to multiple partitions (and topics!) atomically.\n163:  * </p>\n164:  * <p>\n165:  * From Kafka 3.0, the <code>enable.idempotence</code> configuration defaults to true. When enabling idempotence,\n166:  * <code>retries</code> config will default to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code> and the <code>acks</code> config will\n167:  * default to <code>all</code>. There are no API changes for the idempotent producer, so existing applications will\n168:  * not need to be modified to take advantage of this feature.\n169:  * </p>\n170:  * <p>\n171:  * To take advantage of the idempotent producer, it is imperative to avoid application level re-sends since these cannot\n172:  * be de-duplicated. As such, if an application enables idempotence, it is recommended to leave the <code>retries</code>\n173:  * config unset, as it will be defaulted to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>. Additionally, if a {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\n174:  * returns an error even with infinite retries (for instance if the message expires in the buffer before being sent),\n175:  * then it is recommended to shut down the producer and check the contents of the last produced message to ensure that\n176:  * it is not duplicated. Finally, the producer can only guarantee idempotence for messages sent within a single session.\n177:  * </p>\n178:  * <p>To use the transactional producer and the attendant APIs, you must set the <code>transactional.id</code>\n179:  * configuration property. If the <code>transactional.id</code> is set, idempotence is automatically enabled along with\n180:  * the producer configs which idempotence depends on. Further, topics which are included in transactions should be configured\n181:  * for durability. In particular, the <code>replication.factor</code> should be at least <code>3</code>, and the\n182:  * <code>min.insync.replicas</code> for these topics should be set to 2. Finally, in order for transactional guarantees\n183:  * to be realized from end-to-end, the consumers must be configured to read only committed messages as well.\n184:  * </p>\n185:  * <p>\n186:  * The purpose of the <code>transactional.id</code> is to enable transaction recovery across multiple sessions of a\n187:  * single producer instance. It would typically be derived from the shard identifier in a partitioned, stateful, application.\n188:  * As such, it should be unique to each producer instance running within a partitioned application.\n189:  * </p>\n190:  * <p>All the new transactional APIs are blocking and will throw exceptions on failure. The example\n191:  * below illustrates how the new APIs are meant to be used. It is similar to the example above, except that all\n192:  * 100 messages are part of a single transaction.\n193:  * </p>\n194:  * <p>\n195:  * <pre>\n196:  * {@code\n197:  * Properties props = new Properties();\n198:  * props.put(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n199:  * props.put(\"transactional.id\", \"my-transactional-id\");\n200:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props, new StringSerializer(), new StringSerializer());\n201:  *\n202:  * producer.initTransactions();\n203:  *\n204:  * try {\n205:  *     producer.beginTransaction();\n206:  *     for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\n207:  *         producer.send(new ProducerRecord<>(\"my-topic\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\n208:  *     producer.commitTransaction();\n209:  * } catch (ProducerFencedException | OutOfOrderSequenceException | AuthorizationException e) {\n210:  *     // We can't recover from these exceptions, so our only option is to close the producer and exit.\n211:  *     producer.close();\n212:  * } catch (KafkaException e) {\n213:  *     // For all other exceptions, just abort the transaction and try again.\n214:  *     producer.abortTransaction();\n215:  * }\n216:  * producer.close();\n217:  * } </pre>\n218:  * </p>\n219:  * <p>\n220:  * As is hinted at in the example, there can be only one open transaction per producer. All messages sent between the\n221:  * {@link #beginTransaction()} and {@link #commitTransaction()} calls will be part of a single transaction. When the\n222:  * <code>transactional.id</code> is specified, all messages sent by the producer must be part of a transaction.\n223:  * </p>\n224:  * <p>\n225:  * The transactional producer uses exceptions to communicate error states. In particular, it is not required\n226:  * to specify callbacks for <code>producer.send()</code> or to call <code>.get()</code> on the returned Future: a\n227:  * <code>KafkaException</code> would be thrown if any of the\n228:  * <code>producer.send()</code> or transactional calls hit an irrecoverable error during a transaction. See the {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\n229:  * documentation for more details about detecting errors from a transactional send.\n230:  * </p>\n231:  * </p>By calling\n232:  * <code>producer.abortTransaction()</code> upon receiving a <code>KafkaException</code> we can ensure that any\n233:  * successful writes are marked as aborted, hence keeping the transactional guarantees.\n234:  * </p>\n235:  * <p>\n236:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n237:  * certain client features.  For instance, the transactional APIs need broker versions 0.11.0 or later. You will receive an\n238:  * <code>UnsupportedVersionException</code> when invoking an API that is not available in the running broker version.\n239:  * </p>\n240:  */\n241: public class KafkaProducer<K, V> implements Producer<K, V> {\n242: \n243:     private final Logger log;\n244:     private static final String JMX_PREFIX = \"kafka.producer\";\n245:     public static final String NETWORK_THREAD_PREFIX = \"kafka-producer-network-thread\";\n246:     public static final String PRODUCER_METRIC_GROUP_NAME = \"producer-metrics\";\n247: \n248:     private final String clientId;\n249:     // Visible for testing\n250:     final Metrics metrics;\n251:     private final KafkaProducerMetrics producerMetrics;\n252:     private final Plugin<Partitioner> partitionerPlugin;\n253:     private final int maxRequestSize;\n254:     private final long totalMemorySize;\n255:     private final ProducerMetadata metadata;\n256:     private final RecordAccumulator accumulator;\n257:     private final Sender sender;\n258:     private final Sender.SenderThread ioThread;\n259:     private final Compression compression;\n260:     private final Sensor errors;\n261:     private final Time time;\n262:     private final Plugin<Serializer<K>> keySerializerPlugin;\n263:     private final Plugin<Serializer<V>> valueSerializerPlugin;\n264:     private final ProducerConfig producerConfig;\n265:     private final long maxBlockTimeMs;\n266:     private final boolean partitionerIgnoreKeys;\n267:     private final ProducerInterceptors<K, V> interceptors;\n268:     private final ApiVersions apiVersions;\n269:     private final TransactionManager transactionManager;\n270:     // Init value is needed to avoid NPE in case of exception raised in the constructor\n271:     private Optional<ClientTelemetryReporter> clientTelemetryReporter = Optional.empty();\n272: \n273:     /**\n274:      * A producer is instantiated by providing a set of key-value pairs as configuration. Invoking {@link java.util.concurrent.Future#get()\\n853:      * get()} on this future will block until the associated request completes and then return the metadata for the record\\n854:      * or throw any exception that occurred while sending the record.\\n855:      * <p>\\n856:      * If you want to simulate a simple blocking call you can call the <code>get()</code> method immediately:\\n857:      *\\n858:      * <pre>\\n859:      * {@code\\n860:      * byte[] key = \\\"key\\\".getBytes();\\n861:      * byte[] value = \\\"value\\\".getBytes();\\n862:      * ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]> record = new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(\\\"my-topic\\\", key, value)\\n863:      * producer.send(record).get();\\n864:      * }</pre>\\n865:      * <p>\\n866:      * Fully non-blocking usage can make use of the {@link Callback} parameter to provide a callback that\\n867:      * will be invoked when the request is complete.\\n868:      *\\n869:      * <pre>\\n870:      * {@code\\n871:      * ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]> record = new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(\\\"the-topic\\\", key, value);\\n872:      * producer.send(myRecord,\\n873:      *               new Callback() {\\n874:      *                   public void onCompletion(RecordMetadata metadata, Exception e) {\\n875:      *                       if(e != null) {\\n876:      *                          e.printStackTrace();\\n877:      *                       } else {\\n878:      *                          System.out.println(\\\"The offset of the record we just sent is: \\\" + metadata.offset());\\n879:      *                       }\\n880:      *                   }\\n881:      *               });\\n882:      * }\\n883:      * </pre>\\n884:      *\\n885:      * Callbacks for records being sent to the same partition are guaranteed to execute in order. The key components are the serializer, partitioner, RecordAccumulator for batching, and the Sender thread for network transmission.\n\n### Detailed Flow\n\n**1. Serialization and Partitioning**\n- `KafkaProducer.send(ProducerRecord<K, V> record)` at line 941 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java` calls `doSend()`\n- `doSend()` (line 974):\n  - Runs ProducerInterceptors.onSend() to allow interceptors to modify records\n  - Gets cluster metadata via `waitOnMetadata()` (line 988)\n  - Serializes the key using `keySerializerPlugin.get().serialize()` (line 999)\n  - Serializes the value using `valueSerializerPlugin.get().serialize()` (line 1007)\n  - Determines partition via `partition()` method (line 1017) which applies the configured Partitioner\n  - Estimates record size with `AbstractRecords.estimateSizeInBytesUpperBound()` (line 1022)\n\n**2. Batching in RecordAccumulator**\n- `RecordAccumulator.append()` is called at line 1029 with serialized key, value, and partition info\n- The RecordAccumulator maintains per-partition queues of `ProducerBatch` objects\n- Key batching logic in `append()` (line 275 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java`):\n  - Gets or creates a TopicInfo for the topic\n  - Determines effective partition using BuiltInPartitioner if partition was unknown\n  - Checks for in-progress batches in partition queue via `tryAppend()` (line 319)\n  - If no suitable batch exists, allocates a buffer via `BufferPool.allocate()` (line 333)\n  - Creates new batch via `appendNewBatch()` (line 345):\n    - Allocates a `MemoryRecordsBuilder` (line 393)\n    - Creates `ProducerBatch` wrapping the builder (line 394)\n    - Adds batch to incomplete batches queue via `incomplete.add()` (line 399)\n  - Returns `RecordAppendResult` containing future for this record's metadata\n\n**3. Batching Triggers**\n- Back in `doSend()` (line 1041), if `result.batchIsFull || result.newBatchCreated`, the Sender thread is awakened via `sender.wakeup()` (line 1043)\n- Batches become ready to send when:\n  - Batch is full (reaches configured `batch.size`)\n  - `linger.ms` timeout expires\n  - `flush()` is called\n\n**4. Sender Thread Transmission**\n- The Sender thread runs in `Sender.run()` (line 236 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`)\n- Main loop calls `runOnce()` repeatedly (line 242)\n- `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` (line 339)\n- `sendProducerData()` (line 357):\n  - Fetches metadata snapshot via `metadata.fetchMetadataSnapshot()` (line 358)\n  - Calls `accumulator.ready()` to get list of ready partitions with data (line 360)\n  - Requests metadata update for partitions with unknown leaders (lines 363-372)\n  - Removes nodes that aren't ready to send (lines 376-392)\n  - Drains batches via `accumulator.drain()` (line 395) - groups batches by destination broker node\n  - Calls `sendProduceRequests()` (line 442)\n\n**5. Network Request Building and Sending**\n- `sendProduceRequests()` (line 856):\n  - Iterates through each node (destination broker) and calls `sendProduceRequest()` for each\n- `sendProduceRequest()` (line 864):\n  - Groups batches by topic-partition (line 868)\n  - Extracts MemoryRecords from each batch (line 874)\n  - Builds ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection (line 871-886)\n  - Creates `ProduceRequest.Builder` with acks, timeout, and optional transactional ID (lines 897-904)\n  - Creates `ClientRequest` via `client.newClientRequest()` (line 912)\n  - Sends request via `client.send()` (line 914)\n  - Registers response callback `handleProduceResponse()` (line 909)\n\n### Key Configuration Parameters\n- **batch.size**: Threshold at which batches are sent (default 16KB)\n- **linger.ms**: Time to wait for batching before sending (default 0ms)\n- **buffer.memory**: Total memory for buffering (default 32MB)\n- **acks**: Producer acks requirement (-1/all for full replication, 1 for leader only, 0 for none)\n- **compression.type**: Compression applied to batch (none, gzip, snappy, lz4, zstd)\n\n## Q2: Broker-Side Append and Replication\n\n### Overview\nWhen a Produce request arrives at the broker, it follows a precise sequence: routing to the partition leader, validating transaction state, appending to the local log, and coordinating replication to follower replicas.\n\n### Detailed Flow\n\n**1. Request Routing to Partition**\n- The broker's network processor receives the ProduceRequest\n- `ReplicaManager.handleProduceAppend()` is called (line 731 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaManager.scala`) if transactional verification is needed, or `appendRecords()` is called directly (line 674)\n- `handleProduceAppend()` (line 731):\n  - Wraps responseCallback to run on request handler thread\n  - Calls `appendRecords()` with wrapped callback (line 674)\n\n**2. Local Log Append**\n- `appendRecords()` (line 674):\n  - Validates required acks value (line 683)\n  - Calls `appendRecordsToLeader()` to append to local log (line 688)\n  - Builds produce partition status (line 698)\n  - Calls `maybeAddDelayedProduce()` to handle replication waits (line 704)\n\n- `appendRecordsToLeader()` (line 627):\n  - Calls `appendToLocalLog()` to perform the actual append (line 637)\n  - Returns map of `TopicIdPartition` to `LogAppendResult`\n  - Calls `addCompletePurgatoryAction()` to trigger delayed produce completions (line 647)\n\n- `appendToLocalLog()` (line 1370):\n  - For each topic-partition, retrieves the Partition object via `getPartitionOrException()` (line 1407)\n  - Calls `partition.appendRecordsToLeader()` (line 1408)\n  - Records statistics (bytes/messages in rate, latency)\n  - Wraps in `LogAppendResult` containing the `LogAppendInfo`\n\n**3. Partition-Level Append with Replication Coordination**\n- `Partition.appendRecordsToLeader()` (line 1361 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala`):\n  - Acquires read lock on leaderIsrUpdateLock (line 1363)\n  - Gets leader log via `leaderLogIfLocal` (line 1364)\n  - Validates ISR size against min.insync.replicas (line 1370)\n  - Calls `leaderLog.appendAsLeader()` to append to UnifiedLog (line 1376)\n  - Checks if high water mark should be incremented via `maybeIncrementLeaderHW()` (line 1379)\n  - Returns LogAppendInfo with high water mark change information (line 1387)\n\n**4. UnifiedLog Append**\n- `UnifiedLog.appendAsLeader()` (in `storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/log/UnifiedLog.java`):\n  - Validates record batch magic version\n  - Assigns offsets to messages\n  - Writes records to disk via memory-mapped files\n  - Returns `LogAppendInfo` containing:\n    - First offset: lowest offset in batch\n    - Last offset: highest offset in batch\n    - Log append time: broker timestamp when appended\n    - Number of messages\n    - Validation stats\n\n**5. Replication to Followers**\n- Replication is handled asynchronously after local append\n- `ReplicaFetcherThread` on each follower pulls from leader (in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherThread.scala`)\n- Follower sends FetchRequest to leader specifying offset to fetch from\n- Leader returns messages after local log append\n- Follower receives response and calls `Partition.appendRecordsToFollowerOrFutureReplica()` (line 1331 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala`)\n- Follower appends received messages and updates its high water mark\n- As followers acknowledge the append, ISR is maintained\n\n**6. Producer Response**\n- `maybeAddDelayedProduce()` (line 704):\n  - Creates `DelayedProduce` operation waiting for replication acks\n  - If `requiredAcks == -1` (all replicas), waits for all in-sync replicas to acknowledge\n  - If `requiredAcks == 1` (leader), responds immediately after local append\n  - If `requiredAcks == 0` (none), responds after network send\n- `handleProduceResponse()` in Sender (line 568 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`):\n  - Parses ProduceResponse containing base offset and log append time for each partition\n  - For each batch, calls `completeBatch()` to resolve the Future with metadata\n  - ProducerCallback is invoked with RecordMetadata or error\n\n## Q3: Consumer-Side Fetch and Delivery\n\n### Overview\nWhen a consumer calls `poll()`, it retrieves messages previously appended to the broker via a coordinated fetch process, deserializes them, and manages offset commits.\n\n### Detailed Flow\n\n**1. Poll Entry Point**\n- `KafkaConsumer.poll(Duration timeout)` (line 894 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java`):\n  - Delegates to internal delegate (ClassicKafkaConsumer or AsyncKafkaConsumer)\n  - Ultimately calls `Fetcher.sendFetches()` (line 105 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/Fetcher.java`)\n\n**2. Fetch Request Building**\n- `Fetcher.sendFetches()` (line 105):\n  - Calls `prepareFetchRequests()` which groups subscribed partitions by broker leader\n  - Returns Map<Node, FetchSessionHandler.FetchRequestData> with each broker's partitions\n  - Calls `sendFetchesInternal()` (line 107) for each fetch request\n\n- `sendFetchesInternal()` (line 184):\n  - For each broker/FetchRequestData pair:\n    - Creates `FetchRequest.Builder` via `createFetchRequest()` (line 192)\n    - Sends request via `client.send()` (line 193)\n    - Registers listener callbacks:\n      - `handleFetchSuccess()` on success (line 111)\n      - `handleFetchFailure()` on failure (line 116)\n\n**3. Fetch Request Details**\n- FetchRequest includes:\n  - Replica ID (consumer uses replica ID -1)\n  - For each partition:\n    - Fetch offset (where consumer left off)\n    - Max bytes to return\n    - Current leader epoch (for fencing detection)\n  - Isolation level (read_committed or read_uncommitted)\n  - Min bytes and max wait time (for batching at broker)\n\n**4. Broker-Side Fetch Processing**\n- `Partition.fetchRecords()` (line 1414 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala`):\n  - Verifies consumer is authorized to read from partition\n  - Calls `readFromLocalLog()` which calls `readRecords()` (line 1423-1431)\n  - Returns `LogReadInfo` containing:\n    - MemoryRecords: serialized messages from log\n    - High water mark or last stable offset (depending on isolation level)\n\n**5. Response and Deserialization**\n- `handleFetchSuccess()` in Fetcher:\n  - Parses FetchResponse for each partition\n  - Extracts MemoryRecords containing RecordBatches\n  - Calls `FetchCollector.collectFetch()` (line 145)\n\n- `FetchCollector.collectFetch()`:\n  - For each RecordBatch in MemoryRecords:\n    - Deserializes each Record:\n      - Key deserialization via `keyDeserializerPlugin.get().deserialize()`\n      - Value deserialization via `valueDeserializerPlugin.get().deserialize()`\n    - Creates `ConsumerRecord` with:\n      - Topic, partition, offset\n      - Timestamp (from batch or message)\n      - Deserialized key and value\n      - Headers\n      - Leader epoch\n  - Buffers records in consumer's fetch buffer\n  - Maintains high water mark for each partition\n\n**6. Record Delivery to Application**\n- `KafkaConsumer.poll()` returns `ConsumerRecords<K, V>` containing:\n  - Map of TopicPartition to ConsumerRecord lists\n  - Application iterates over records\n  - Application can call `commitSync()` or `commitAsync()` to commit offsets\n\n**7. Offset Commits**\n- Offset commits can occur:\n  - Explicitly via `commitSync(offsets)` / `commitAsync(offsets, callback)`\n  - Implicitly via `enable.auto.commit=true` based on `auto.commit.interval.ms`\n  - As part of consumer group rebalancing\n- Offset is sent to group coordinator broker and stored in `__consumer_offsets` topic\n- Next `poll()` call fetches from committed offset, achieving exactly-once message delivery with retries\n\n## Q4: End-to-End Transformation Points\n\n### Transformation Point Sequence\n\n**1. User Object → Serialized Bytes (Producer)**\n- **Location**: `KafkaProducer.doSend()`, lines 999 and 1007\n- **File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java`\n- **Operation**:\n  - Key: `keySerializerPlugin.get().serialize(record.topic(), record.headers(), record.key())`\n  - Value: `valueSerializerPlugin.get().serialize(record.topic(), record.headers(), record.value())`\n- **Change**: Object instances (String, byte[], Avro, JSON, etc.) converted to byte arrays\n- **Purpose**: Network-safe binary representation\n\n**2. The key components are the serializer, partitioner, RecordAccumulator for batching, and the Sender thread for network transmission.\n\n### Detailed Flow\n\n**1. Serialization and Partitioning**\n- `KafkaProducer.send(ProducerRecord<K, V> record)` at line 941 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java` calls `doSend()`\n- `doSend()` (line 974):\n  - Runs ProducerInterceptors.onSend() to allow interceptors to modify records\n  - Gets cluster metadata via `waitOnMetadata()` (line 988)\n  - Serializes the key using `keySerializerPlugin.get().serialize()` (line 999)\n  - Serializes the value using `valueSerializerPlugin.get().serialize()` (line 1007)\n  - Determines partition via `partition()` method (line 1017) which applies the configured Partitioner\n  - Estimates record size with `AbstractRecords.estimateSizeInBytesUpperBound()` (line 1022)\n\n**2. Batching in RecordAccumulator**\n- `RecordAccumulator.append()` is called at line 1029 with serialized key, value, and partition info\n- The RecordAccumulator maintains per-partition queues of `ProducerBatch` objects\n- Key batching logic in `append()` (line 275 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java`):\n  - Gets or creates a TopicInfo for the topic\n  - Determines effective partition using BuiltInPartitioner if partition was unknown\n  - Checks for in-progress batches in partition queue via `tryAppend()` (line 319)\n  - If no suitable batch exists, allocates a buffer via `BufferPool.allocate()` (line 333)\n  - Creates new batch via `appendNewBatch()` (line 345):\n    - Allocates a `MemoryRecordsBuilder` (line 393)\n    - Creates `ProducerBatch` wrapping the builder (line 394)\n    - Adds batch to incomplete batches queue via `incomplete.add()` (line 399)\n  - Returns `RecordAppendResult` containing future for this record's metadata\n\n**3. Batching Triggers**\n- Back in `doSend()` (line 1041), if `result.batchIsFull || result.newBatchCreated`, the Sender thread is awakened via `sender.wakeup()` (line 1043)\n- Batches become ready to send when:\n  - Batch is full (reaches configured `batch.size`)\n  - `linger.ms` timeout expires\n  - `flush()` is called\n\n**4. Sender Thread Transmission**\n- The Sender thread runs in `Sender.run()` (line 236 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`)\n- Main loop calls `runOnce()` repeatedly (line 242)\n- `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` (line 339)\n- `sendProducerData()` (line 357):\n  - Fetches metadata snapshot via `metadata.fetchMetadataSnapshot()` (line 358)\n  - Calls `accumulator.ready()` to get list of ready partitions with data (line 360)\n  - Requests metadata update for partitions with unknown leaders (lines 363-372)\n  - Removes nodes that aren't ready to send (lines 376-392)\n  - Drains batches via `accumulator.drain()` (line 395) - groups batches by destination broker node\n  - Calls `sendProduceRequests()` (line 442)\n\n**5. Network Request Building and Sending**\n- `sendProduceRequests()` (line 856):\n  - Iterates through each node (destination broker) and calls `sendProduceRequest()` for each\n- `sendProduceRequest()` (line 864):\n  - Groups batches by topic-partition (line 868)\n  - Extracts MemoryRecords from each batch (line 874)\n  - Builds ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection (line 871-886)\n  - Creates `ProduceRequest.Builder` with acks, timeout, and optional transactional ID (lines 897-904)\n  - Creates `ClientRequest` via `client.newClientRequest()` (line 912)\n  - Sends request via `client.send()` (line 914)\n  - Registers response callback `handleProduceResponse()` (line 909)\n\n### Key Configuration Parameters\n- **batch.size**: Threshold at which batches are sent (default 16KB)\n- **linger.ms**: Time to wait for batching before sending (default 0ms)\n- **buffer.memory**: Total memory for buffering (default 32MB)\n- **acks**: Producer acks requirement (-1/all for full replication, 1 for leader only, 0 for none)\n- **compression.type**: Compression applied to batch (none, gzip, snappy, lz4, zstd)\n\n## Q2: Broker-Side Append and Replication\n\n### Overview\nWhen a Produce request arrives at the broker, it follows a precise sequence: routing to the partition leader, validating transaction state, appending to the local log, and coordinating replication to follower replicas.\n\n### Detailed Flow\n\n**1. Request Routing to Partition**\n- The broker's network processor receives the ProduceRequest\n- `ReplicaManager.handleProduceAppend()` is called (line 731 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaManager.scala`) if transactional verification is needed, or `appendRecords()` is called directly (line 674)\n- `handleProduceAppend()` (line 731):\n  - Wraps responseCallback to run on request handler thread\n  - Calls `appendRecords()` with wrapped callback (line 674)\n\n**2. Local Log Append**\n- `appendRecords()` (line 674):\n  - Validates required acks value (line 683)\n  - Calls `appendRecordsToLeader()` to append to local log (line 688)\n  - Builds produce partition status (line 698)\n  - Calls `maybeAddDelayedProduce()` to handle replication waits (line 704)\n\n- `appendRecordsToLeader()` (line 627):\n  - Calls `appendToLocalLog()` to perform the actual append (line 637)\n  - Returns map of `TopicIdPartition` to `LogAppendResult`\n  - Calls `addCompletePurgatoryAction()` to trigger delayed produce completions (line 647)\n\n- `appendToLocalLog()` (line 1370):\n  - For each topic-partition, retrieves the Partition object via `getPartitionOrException()` (line 1407)\n  - Calls `partition.appendRecordsToLeader()` (line 1408)\n  - Records statistics (bytes/messages in rate, latency)\n  - Wraps in `LogAppendResult` containing the `LogAppendInfo`\n\n**3. Partition-Level Append with Replication Coordination**\n- `Partition.appendRecordsToLeader()` (line 1361 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala`):\n  - Acquires read lock on leaderIsrUpdateLock (line 1363)\n  - Gets leader log via `leaderLogIfLocal` (line 1364)\n  - Validates ISR size against min.insync.replicas (line 1370)\n  - Calls `leaderLog.appendAsLeader()` to append to UnifiedLog (line 1376)\n  - Checks if high water mark should be incremented via `maybeIncrementLeaderHW()` (line 1379)\n  - Returns LogAppendInfo with high water mark change information (line 1387)\n\n**4. UnifiedLog Append**\n- `UnifiedLog.appendAsLeader()` (in `storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/log/UnifiedLog.java`):\n  - Validates record batch magic version\n  - Assigns offsets to messages\n  - Writes records to disk via memory-mapped files\n  - Returns `LogAppendInfo` containing:\n    - First offset: lowest offset in batch\n    - Last offset: highest offset in batch\n    - Log append time: broker timestamp when appended\n    - Number of messages\n    - Validation stats\n\n**5. Replication to Followers**\n- Replication is handled asynchronously after local append\n- `ReplicaFetcherThread` on each follower pulls from leader (in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherThread.scala`)\n- Follower sends FetchRequest to leader specifying offset to fetch from\n- Leader returns messages after local log append\n- Follower receives response and calls `Partition.appendRecordsToFollowerOrFutureReplica()` (line 1331 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala`)\n- Follower appends received messages and updates its high water mark\n- As followers acknowledge the append, ISR is maintained\n\n**6. Producer Response**\n- `maybeAddDelayedProduce()` (line 704):\n  - Creates `DelayedProduce` operation waiting for replication acks\n  - If `requiredAcks == -1` (all replicas), waits for all in-sync replicas to acknowledge\n  - If `requiredAcks == 1` (leader), responds immediately after local append\n  - If `requiredAcks == 0` (none), responds after network send\n- `handleProduceResponse()` in Sender (line 568 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`):\n  - Parses ProduceResponse containing base offset and log append time for each partition\n  - For each batch, calls `completeBatch()` to resolve the Future with metadata\n  - ProducerCallback is invoked with RecordMetadata or error\n\n## Q3: Consumer-Side Fetch and Delivery\n\n### Overview\nWhen a consumer calls `poll()`, it retrieves messages previously appended to the broker via a coordinated fetch process, deserializes them, and manages offset commits.\n\n### Detailed Flow\n\n**1. Poll Entry Point**\n- `KafkaConsumer.poll(Duration timeout)` (line 894 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java`):\n  - Delegates to internal delegate (ClassicKafkaConsumer or AsyncKafkaConsumer)\n  - Ultimately calls `Fetcher.sendFetches()` (line 105 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/Fetcher.java`)\n\n**2. Fetch Request Building**\n- `Fetcher.sendFetches()` (line 105):\n  - Calls `prepareFetchRequests()` which groups subscribed partitions by broker leader\n  - Returns Map<Node, FetchSessionHandler.FetchRequestData> with each broker's partitions\n  - Calls `sendFetchesInternal()` (line 107) for each fetch request\n\n- `sendFetchesInternal()` (line 184):\n  - For each broker/FetchRequestData pair:\n    - Creates `FetchRequest.Builder` via `createFetchRequest()` (line 192)\n    - Sends request via `client.send()` (line 193)\n    - Registers listener callbacks:\n      - `handleFetchSuccess()` on success (line 111)\n      - `handleFetchFailure()` on failure (line 116)\n\n**3. Fetch Request Details**\n- FetchRequest includes:\n  - Replica ID (consumer uses replica ID -1)\n  - For each partition:\n    - Fetch offset (where consumer left off)\n    - Max bytes to return\n    - Current leader epoch (for fencing detection)\n  - Isolation level (read_committed or read_uncommitted)\n  - Min bytes and max wait time (for batching at broker)\n\n**4. Broker-Side Fetch Processing**\n- `Partition.fetchRecords()` (line 1414 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala`):\n  - Verifies consumer is authorized to read from partition\n  - Calls `readFromLocalLog()` which calls `readRecords()` (line 1423-1431)\n  - Returns `LogReadInfo` containing:\n    - MemoryRecords: serialized messages from log\n    - High water mark or last stable offset (depending on isolation level)\n\n**5. Record Delivery to Application**\n- `KafkaConsumer.poll()` returns `ConsumerRecords<K, V>` containing:\n  - Map of TopicPartition to ConsumerRecord lists\n  - Application iterates over records\n  - Application can call `commitSync()` or `commitAsync()` to commit offsets\n\n**7. Offset Commits**\n- Offset commits can occur:\n  - Explicitly via `commitSync(offsets)` / `commitAsync(offsets, callback)`\n  - Implicitly via `enable.auto.commit=true` based on `auto.commit.interval.ms`\n  - As part of consumer group rebalancing\n- Offset is sent to group coordinator broker and stored in `__consumer_offsets` topic\n- Next `poll()` call fetches from committed offset, achieving exactly-once message delivery with retries\n\n## Q4: End-to-End Transformation Points\n\n### Transformation Point Sequence\n\n**1. I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the Kafka message lifecycle and written the results to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.\n\n## Summary\n\nThe investigation documents the complete path of a single message through Kafka's architecture:\n\n### **Q1: Producer-Side Batching & Transmission**\n- Messages are serialized (key & value) and partitioned in `KafkaProducer.doSend()`\n- `RecordAccumulator` batches messages into `ProducerBatch` objects with compression\n- Sender thread sends batches as `ProduceRequest` when full, `linger.ms` expires, or `flush()` called\n- Compression
